<p><b>Riverdale</b> is a residential <a href="/wiki/Neighborhood" class="mw-redirect" title="Neighborhood">neighborhood</a> in the northwest portion of <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">the Bronx</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough (New York City)">borough</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. Riverdale, which has a population of 47,850 as of the <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">2000 United States Census</a>, contains the northernmost point in New York City. Riverdale's boundaries are disputed, but it is commonly agreed to be bordered by <a href="/wiki/Yonkers,_New_York" title="Yonkers, New York">Yonkers</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Van_Cortlandt_Park" title="Van Cortlandt Park">Van Cortlandt Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Bronx)" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadway (Bronx)">Broadway</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Kingsbridge,_Bronx" title="Kingsbridge, Bronx">Kingsbridge</a> neighborhood to the southeast, the <a href="/wiki/Harlem_River" title="Harlem River">Harlem River</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil,_Bronx" title="Spuyten Duyvil, Bronx">Spuyten Duyvil</a> neighborhood to the south, and the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> to the west. Riverdale Avenue is the primary thoroughfare through Riverdale.<sup id="cite_ref-encnyc_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnyc-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boundaries_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boundaries-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boundaries_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boundaries-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The neighborhood is part of <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Community_Board_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronx Community Board 8">Bronx Community District 8</a>, and its ZIP Codes include 10463 and 10471. The area is patrolled by the 50th Precinct of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">New York City Police Department</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYCPlanningBx8_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYCPlanningBx8-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1642, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Van_Corlaer" title="Anthony Van Corlaer">Anthony Van Corlaer</a> died while attempting to swim across the Hudson from nearby <a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil,_Bronx" title="Spuyten Duyvil, Bronx">Spuyten Duyvil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> A witness to Van Corlaer's death stated that "the devil" in the shape of a giant fish swam up and proceeded to "seize the sturdy Anthony by the leg and drag him beneath the waves." This may be the earliest recorded shark attack in the New World.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>  In the late 17th century, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Philipse" title="Frederick Philipse">Frederick Philipse</a>, the lord of <a href="/wiki/Philipse_Manor_Hall_State_Historic_Site" title="Philipse Manor Hall State Historic Site">Philipse Manor</a> in Westchester County, received permission to construct a bridge across <a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil_Creek" title="Spuyten Duyvil Creek">Spuyten Duyvil Creek</a> and charge tolls.  "King's Bridge", which was located roughly south of and parallel to where West 230th Street lies today, opened in 1693.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Early in its residential development, Riverdale was a 19th-century estate district where many of Manhattan's moguls built their country estates; for example, in northern Riverdale, what is now <a href="/wiki/Fieldston,_Bronx" title="Fieldston, Bronx">Fieldston</a> was part of the estate of Major <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Delafield" title="Joseph Delafield">Joseph Delafield</a>, who purchased 250 acres (100&#160;ha) in 1829, and named it after his family's estate in England. At the turn of the century, the new popularity of railroad commute enabled wealthy businessmen to make Riverdale their year-round residence. Fieldston, owned by a private association, is a particularly intact example of a turn-of-the century upper class suburb. The <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Hill,_Bronx" title="Hudson Hill, Bronx">Hudson Hill</a> neighborhood retains many of its historic mansions. Riverdale's elite private schools and historic churches also reflect this past. Development of the neighborhood began in the latter half of the 19th century once the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Central_and_Hudson_River_Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Central and Hudson River Railroad">New York Central and Hudson River Railroad</a> came through.<sup id="cite_ref-encnyc_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnyc-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The tracks originally crossed Spuyten Duyvil Creek and into Manhattan on the west side, but <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Vanderbilt" title="Cornelius Vanderbilt">Cornelius Vanderbilt</a> wanted to consolidate his railroad operations into one terminal. He had tracks laid along the north side of the Harlem River so that trains coming south from Albany could join with the Harlem and New Haven lines and come into Manhattan down the <a href="/wiki/Park_Avenue_main_line" title="Park Avenue main line">Park Avenue main line</a>, along modern-day <a href="/wiki/Park_Avenue" title="Park Avenue">Park Avenue</a>, into his new <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Depot" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Central Depot">Grand Central Depot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> This is the route still used by the <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North Railroad</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Line_(Metro-North)" title="Hudson Line (Metro-North)">Hudson Line</a>.
</p><p>The Delafield family laid out lots in Fieldston in 1909&#160;– the year after the <a href="/wiki/IRT_Broadway%E2%80%93Seventh_Avenue_Line" title="IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line">IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line</a> (present-day <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1_(New_York_City_Subway_service)" title="1 (New York City Subway service)">1</a></span>&#32;train) was extended to <a href="/wiki/Van_Cortlandt_Park%E2%80%93242nd_Street_(IRT_Broadway%E2%80%93Seventh_Avenue_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Cortlandt Park–242nd Street (IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line)">Van Cortlandt Park–242nd Street</a>, intending to develop the land, which at first was called "Delafield Woods". Rather than use a grid plan, civil engineer Albert E. Wheeler, following the suggestions made by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a> and James R. Croes in 1876, designed a street plan which followed the contours of the land and preserved as much of the wooded areas as possible. The first house was begun in 1910 and finished in 1911;<sup id="cite_ref-encnyc_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnyc-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nycland_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nycland-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> by the beginning of the 21st century, Fieldston, a privately owned community, was one of the wealthiest neighborhoods in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-encfieldston_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encfieldston-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Leland Weintraub, the commissioner who moved for the district's creation, noted that "most of the features commonly associated with the American romantic suburb of the mid-19th century", including "a picturesque site, landscaping and architecture; connection to the city by accessible transportation and a layout adapted to the topography" are present in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1928, Genevieve Ludlow Griscom, who was a member of a small religious group called the Outer Court of the Order of the Living Christ, built a 15,000-square-foot (1,400&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) mansion at 360 West 253rd Street &#8211; also addressed as 5200 Longview Place &#8211; for the express purpose of housing Jesus Christ when the <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">Second Coming</a> occurred.  After being derelict for a number of years under successive owners, the mansion was bought in 1987 by entrepreneur Jerry Galuten, who renovated it into an even more opulent 17 room home. After being on- and off-the market for eight years, with an asking price as high as $15 million, the house sold in January 2017 for $6.25 million.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As the 20th century progressed, upscale apartment buildings and smaller houses were added to the neighborhood. To this day, Riverdale continues to maintain its character as an affluent enclave in the city of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The rich history of Riverdale has led to the creation of the Riverdale Historic District.
</p><p>In May 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> ran a sting operation to prevent a <a href="/wiki/2009_New_York_terrorism_plot" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 New York terrorism plot">bombing plot</a> in which two Riverdale <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> were the suggested targets.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>  This followed a <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">Molotov cocktail</a> attack in 2000 on a different Riverdale synagogue<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/1989_firebombing_of_the_Riverdale_Press" title="1989 firebombing of the Riverdale Press">1989 firebombing of the Riverdale Press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 26, 2010, the <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> confirmed that an EF1 tornado had hit Riverdale the day before. There were no fatalities, but seven people were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 1, 2013, <a href="/wiki/December_2013_Spuyten_Duyvil_derailment" title="December 2013 Spuyten Duyvil derailment">a train derailment</a> near <a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil_(Metro-North_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spuyten Duyvil (Metro-North station)">Spuyten Duyvil station</a> resulted in four deaths and over 70 injuries, of which 11 were critical.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riverdale covers about 3 square miles (7.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) in area. It has one of the highest elevations in New York City, affording it views of the <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Bridge" title="George Washington Bridge">George Washington Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Palisades" class="mw-redirect" title="New Jersey Palisades">New Jersey Palisades</a>. It is also noted for the numerous parks and expanses of greenery and original forest that complement its hilly landscape. The neighborhood is bordered on the north by the city of <a href="/wiki/Yonkers,_New_York" title="Yonkers, New York">Yonkers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">Westchester County</a>, and on the west by the Hudson River, but its eastern and southern boundaries are frequently disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-encnyc_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encnyc-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boundaries_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boundaries-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/AIA_Guide_to_New_York_City" title="AIA Guide to New York City">AIA Guide to New York City</a></i> gives Broadway as the eastern boundary, and the <a href="/wiki/Harlem_River" title="Harlem River">Harlem River</a> as the southern.<sup id="cite_ref-aia5_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aia5-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> There are several long-debated subsections of Riverdale:<sup id="cite_ref-boundaries_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boundaries-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:229px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RiverdaleBronxNY.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/RiverdaleBronxNY.jpg" decoding="async" width="227" height="230" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="227" data-file-height="230" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RiverdaleBronxNY.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of Riverdale within the Bronx</div></div></div>
<ul><li><b>Central Riverdale</b> (the "<a href="/wiki/Downtown" title="Downtown">downtown</a>" area of Riverdale&#160;– from Manhattan College Parkway to West 232nd Street and from the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson_Parkway" title="Henry Hudson Parkway">Henry Hudson Parkway</a> to Riverdale Avenue and Waldo Avenue)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Fieldston,_Bronx" title="Fieldston, Bronx">Fieldston</a></b> (Riverdale south of West 250th Street, east of the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson_Parkway" title="Henry Hudson Parkway">Henry Hudson Parkway</a>, north of Manhattan College Parkway, and west of Tibbett Avenue)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Hudson_Hill,_Bronx" title="Hudson Hill, Bronx">Hudson Hill</a></b> (Riverdale above West 246th Street and west of Henry Hudson Parkway)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/North_Riverdale,_Bronx" title="North Riverdale, Bronx">North Riverdale</a></b> (Riverdale above West 254th Street and west of Fieldston Road)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Mosholu,_Bronx" title="Mosholu, Bronx">Mosholu</a></b> (Riverdale East of Fieldston Road and above West 254th Street, includes Spencer Ave, Huxley Rd, Post Rd, and <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">Broadway</a>)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil,_Bronx" title="Spuyten Duyvil, Bronx">Spuyten Duyvil</a></b> / <b>South Riverdale</b> (the southernmost section of Riverdale, below West 232nd Street or West 239th Street by some definitions. Also included is the business, commercial and shopping district located at West 231`Street and Broadway)</li>
<li><b>Villanova Heights</b> (a sub-division bounded by Fieldston Road on the east, 250th Street on the south, and the Henry Hudson Parkway on the west and north)<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The leafy, scenic enclave of Fieldston was designated a <a href="/wiki/Historic_district" title="Historic district">historic district</a> by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Landmarks_Preservation_Commission" title="New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission">New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-nycland_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nycland-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> There is also a 15-acre Riverdale Historic District in the northwest of the neighborhood, designated in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-nycland_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nycland-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg/250px-Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg/375px-Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg/500px-Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Woodland_path_Wave_Hill_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pathway in <a href="/wiki/Wave_Hill" title="Wave Hill">Wave Hill</a></div></div></div>
<p>Based on data from the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>, the population of Riverdale was 27,860, a change of -153 (-0.5%) from the 28,013 counted in <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">2000</a>. Covering an area of 1,139.68 acres (461.21&#160;ha), the neighborhood had a population density of 24.4 inhabitants per acre (15,600/sq&#160;mi; 6,000/km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-PLP5_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PLP5-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The racial makeup of the neighborhood was 67.5% (18,794) <a href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 7.7% (2,136) <a href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 0.1% (26) <a href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 5.3% (1,468) <a href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0% (4) <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 0.3% (91) from <a href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Race (United States Census)">other races</a>, and 1.6% (446) from two or more races. <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 17.6% (4,895) of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-PLP3A_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PLP3A-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The entirety of Community District 8, which comprises Riverdale, Fieldston, and Kingsbridge, had 102,927 inhabitants as of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Health_and_Mental_Hygiene" title="New York City Department of Health and Mental Hygiene">NYC Health</a>'s 2018 Community Health Profile, with an average life expectancy of 80.9 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2, 20</span></sup> This is about the same as the median life expectancy of 81.2 for all New York City neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-:21_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:21-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>53 (PDF p. 84)</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Most inhabitants are youth and middle-aged adults: 20% are between the ages of between 0–17, 28% between 25–44, and 25% between 45–64. The ratio of college-aged and elderly residents was lower, at 9% and 18% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup>
</p><p>As of 2017, the median <a href="/wiki/Household_income" class="mw-redirect" title="Household income">household income</a> in Community District 8 was $53,986.<sup id="cite_ref-CB8PUMA_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CB8PUMA-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, an estimated 15% of Riverdale residents lived in poverty, compared to 25% in all of the Bronx and 20% in all of New York City. One in eleven residents (9%) were unemployed, compared to 13% in the Bronx and 9% in New York City. Rent burden, or the percentage of residents who have difficulty paying their rent, is 52% in Riverdale, compared to the boroughwide and citywide rates of 58% and 51% respectively. Based on this calculation, as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Riverdale is considered high-income relative to the rest of the city and not <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">gentrifying</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>7</span></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riverdale is home to the modernist landmark Saul Victor house, designed by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Gottlieb" title="Ferdinand Gottlieb">Ferdinand Gottlieb</a> in 1967. Other famous mansions in the Hudson Hill neighborhood include: Greyston (1864), Alderbrook (1880), Stonehurst (1861) and Oaklawn (1863). Since 2005, Central Riverdale has experienced a building boom with the addition of many mid- and high-rise condominium buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> With a median residence value of $579,196 as of 2013, Riverdale is one of the most expensive neighborhoods in New York City and is considered one of the most sought-after residential neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the wider development of Riverdale, housing consisted of large, architecturally distinguished mansions built in the early 20th century, mostly in Georgian- and Tudor-revival styles, which recall scenes of "rural Connecticut" rather than the city.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> These are mostly concentrated in the Fieldston section of Riverdale, known as the estate area. In addition, more affordable pre-war buildings and smaller houses are scattered throughout Riverdale. The 1950s saw the construction of many low-rise (six-story) brick buildings. By the early to mid-1960s, a number of larger brick towers (10–20 stories) started popping up. Many of these full-service buildings featuring doormen were designed by architect Philip Birnbaum, who designed over 300 buildings in the city, including Skyview, the Windsors, and the Whitehall.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1974, a large, fortress-like residential compound and school was established in North Riverdale by the Permanent Mission of the USSR to the United Nations (now the Permanent Mission of the Russian Federation to the UN) to house diplomats and their families. The 20-story building was constructed from the top down, with the upper floors built first.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the 1980s, most of the apartment buildings that were owned by single landlords and rented, were converted into cooperatives. Unlike most of the Bronx, Riverdale is mostly owner-occupied housing. Spuyten Duyvil has the greatest concentration of high rises in Riverdale with the Century, 555 Kappock, and Winston Churchill next to one another. Since 2005, Central Riverdale has experienced a building boom with the addition of many mid- and high-rise condominium buildings that contrast with the older brick style. In August 2008, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a> purchased an almost-completed apartment building near Henry Hudson Parkway for use as faculty housing. 
</p>
<div align="center"><ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 1072px;_width: 1072px;">

		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 260px"><div style="width: 260px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 255px;"><div style="margin:27.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg/225px-4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg/338px-4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg/450px-4695_Independ_Av_Riverdale_jeh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>A house on Independence Avenue
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 260px"><div style="width: 260px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 255px;"><div style="margin:18.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg/225px-5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="225" height="168" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg/338px-5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg/450px-5200_block_of_Palisade_Avenue_year_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Palisade Avenue
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Two weekly newspapers, the <i><a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Press" title="Riverdale Press">Riverdale Press</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Review" title="Riverdale Review">Riverdale Review</a></i>, focus on news of interest to residents of the neighborhood.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_and_crime">Police and crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Police and crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg/275px-Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg" decoding="async" width="275" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg/413px-Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg/550px-Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_Hudson_Parkway_in_Riverdale.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northbound <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson_Parkway" title="Henry Hudson Parkway">Henry Hudson Parkway</a></div></div></div>
<p>Riverdale is patrolled by the 50th Precinct of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">NYPD</a>, located at 3450 Kingsbridge Avenue.<sup id="cite_ref-NYPD_50th_Precinct_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYPD_50th_Precinct-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The 50th Precinct ranked 13th safest out of 69 patrol areas for per-capita crime in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> With a non-fatal assault rate of 40 per 100,000 people, Riverdale's rate of violent crimes per capita is less than that of the city as a whole. The incarceration rate of 225 per 100,000 people is lower than that of the city as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8</span></sup> Riverdale is known for having some of the lowest crime rates in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 50th Precinct has a lower crime rate than in the 1990s, with crimes across all categories having decreased by 81.5% between 1990 and 2018. The precinct saw 7 murders, 15 rapes, 110 robberies, 147 felony assaults, 105 burglaries, 458 grand larcenies, and 97 grand larcenies auto in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_safety">Fire safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fire safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riverdale contains a <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Fire_Department" title="New York City Fire Department">New York City Fire Department</a> (FDNY) fire station, Engine Co. 52/Ladder Co. 52, at 4550 Henry Hudson Parkway East. Engine Co. 52/Ladder Co. 52 is the only firehouse in Riverdale and the northernmost fire station operated by the FDNY.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Preterm_birth" title="Preterm birth">Preterm</a> births are slightly more common in Riverdale than in other places citywide, though teenage births are less common. In Riverdale, there were 89 preterm births per 1,000 live births (compared to 87 per 1,000 citywide), and 13.1 teenage births per 1,000 live births (compared to 19.3 per 1,000 citywide).<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>11</span></sup> Riverdale has a relatively average population of residents who are <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance_coverage_in_the_United_States" title="Health insurance coverage in the United States">uninsured</a>. In 2018, this population of uninsured residents was estimated to be 16%, higher than the citywide rate of 12%.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>14</span></sup>
</p><p>The concentration of <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">fine particulate matter</a>, the deadliest type of <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollutant</a>, in Riverdale is 0.0075 milligrams per cubic metre (7.5<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>−9</sup>&#160;oz/cu&#160;ft), more than the city average.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>9</span></sup> Ten percent of Riverdale residents are <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">smokers</a>, which is lower than the city average of 14% of residents being smokers.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>13</span></sup> In Riverdale, 24% of residents are <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obese</a>, 12% are <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetic</a>, and 28% have <a href="/wiki/Hypertension" title="Hypertension">high blood pressure</a>—compared to the citywide averages of 24%, 11%, and 28% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>16</span></sup> In addition, 21% of children are obese, compared to the citywide average of 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>12</span></sup>
</p><p>Eighty-six percent of residents eat some fruits and vegetables every day, which is less than the city's average of 87%. In 2018, 83% of residents described their health as "good," "very good," or "excellent," higher than the city's average of 78%.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>13</span></sup> For every supermarket in Riverdale, there are 10 <a href="/wiki/Convenience_store" title="Convenience store">bodegas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>10</span></sup>
</p><p>The nearest hospitals are <a href="/wiki/James_J._Peters_VA_Medical_Center" title="James J. Peters VA Medical Center">James J. Peters VA Medical Center</a> in Kingsbridge Heights, <a href="/wiki/North_Central_Bronx_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="North Central Bronx Hospital">North Central Bronx Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montefiore_Medical_Center" title="Montefiore Medical Center">Montefiore Medical Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norwood,_Bronx" title="Norwood, Bronx">Norwood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_offices_and_ZIP_codes">Post offices and ZIP codes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Post offices and ZIP codes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riverdale is located within two <a href="/wiki/ZIP_Code" title="ZIP Code">ZIP Codes</a>. The area north of Manhattan College Parkway and 239th Street is in 10471, while the area south of these two streets is in 10463. While 10471 is entirely in Riverdale, 10463 also covers the adjacent neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Kingsbridge,_Bronx" title="Kingsbridge, Bronx">Kingsbridge, Bronx</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marble_Hill,_Manhattan" title="Marble Hill, Manhattan">Marble Hill, Manhattan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> operates three post offices nearby:
</p>
<ul><li>Riverdale Station – 5951 Riverdale Avenue<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Fieldston Station – 444 West 238th Street<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Spuyten Duyvil Station – 444 West 238th Street<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cmsm_800.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Cmsm_800.jpg/275px-Cmsm_800.jpg" decoding="async" width="275" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Cmsm_800.jpg/413px-Cmsm_800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Cmsm_800.jpg/550px-Cmsm_800.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="599" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cmsm_800.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/College_of_Mount_Saint_Vincent" title="College of Mount Saint Vincent">College of Mount Saint Vincent</a></div></div></div>
<p>Riverdale generally has a similar rate of college-educated residents to the rest of the city. While 45% of residents age 25 and older have a college education or higher, 18% have less than a high school education and 37% are high school graduates or have some college education. By contrast, 26% of Bronx residents and 43% of city residents have a college education or higher.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>6</span></sup> The percentage of Riverdale students excelling in math rose from 21% in 2000 to 48% in 2011, and reading achievement increased from 28% to 33% during the same time period.<sup id="cite_ref-:17_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:17-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Riverdale's rate of elementary school student absenteeism is about the same as the rest of New York City. In Riverdale, 20% of elementary school students missed twenty or more days per <a href="/wiki/School_year" class="mw-redirect" title="School year">school year</a>, higher than the citywide average of 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-:21_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:21-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>24 (PDF p. 55)</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>6</span></sup> Additionally, 78% of high school students in Riverdale graduate on time, higher than the citywide average of 75%.<sup id="cite_ref-CHP2018_28-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHP2018-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>6</span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_schools">Public schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Public schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The public schools are a part of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">New York City Department of Education</a>. The public elementary schools are the Spuyten Duyvil School (P.S. 24)<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and the Robert J. Christen School (P.S. 81).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> There is one zoned public middle and high school in Riverdale: M.S./H.S 141, the <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Kingsbridge_Academy" title="Riverdale Kingsbridge Academy">Riverdale Kingsbridge Academy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Nearby public high schools that serve the community include the <a href="/wiki/Bronx_High_School_of_Science" title="Bronx High School of Science">Bronx High School of Science</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Specialized_high_schools_in_New_York_City" title="Specialized high schools in New York City">specialized high school</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_High_School_(New_York_City)" title="John F. Kennedy High School (New York City)">John F. Kennedy High School Campus</a>, consisting of four separate high schools;<sup id="cite_ref-2016NYCSchoolsCatalog_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016NYCSchoolsCatalog-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and the IN-Tech Academy MS/HS 368, which also contains a middle school.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_schools">Private schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Private schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Riverdale is home to three top-tier private schools: <a href="/wiki/Horace_Mann_School" title="Horace Mann School">Horace Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Country_School" title="Riverdale Country School">Riverdale Country</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ethical_Culture_Fieldston_School" title="Ethical Culture Fieldston School">Fieldston</a>, all members of the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Preparatory_School_League" title="Ivy Preparatory School League">Ivy Preparatory School League</a>; and two Roman Catholic colleges: The <a href="/wiki/College_of_Mount_Saint_Vincent" title="College of Mount Saint Vincent">College of Mount Saint Vincent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_College" title="Manhattan College">Manhattan College</a>.
</p><p>An increase in the Jewish population of the neighborhood in the late twentieth century led to Riverdale now being home to top-ranked <a href="/wiki/Jewish_day_school" title="Jewish day school">Jewish day schools</a>, the <a href="/wiki/SAR_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="SAR Academy">SAR Academy</a>, an elementary school, and the <a href="/wiki/SAR_High_School" title="SAR High School">SAR High School</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva_of_Telshe_Alumni" title="Yeshiva of Telshe Alumni">Yeshiva of Telshe Alumni</a> and Yeshivat Ohavei Torah Rabbinical School. Catholic elementary schools in the area are Visitation School, St. Gabriel's School and <a href="/wiki/St._Margaret_of_Cortona_School" title="St. Margaret of Cortona School">St. Margaret of Cortona School</a>, where President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> received his <a href="/wiki/Confirmation" title="Confirmation">Confirmation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Mission_November_5,_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Russian_Mission_November_5%2C_2012.jpg/250px-Russian_Mission_November_5%2C_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Russian_Mission_November_5%2C_2012.jpg/375px-Russian_Mission_November_5%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Russian_Mission_November_5%2C_2012.jpg/500px-Russian_Mission_November_5%2C_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1392" data-file-height="1476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Mission_November_5,_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian Mission Residency</div></div></div>
<p>The area also has several preschools. Kinneret Day School is a private Jewish day school in Spuyten Duyvil, serving grades K through 8 in addition to pre-school.<sup id="cite_ref-Kinneret_Day_School_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kinneret_Day_School-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Others are BedRock Preschool, the Riverdale Temple Nursery School, Spuyten Duyvil Preschool,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>  SAR Academy (Early Learning Center), Riverdale Nursery School and Family Center,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> the Riverdale Presbyterian Church Nursery School,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and Riverdale Montessori School.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Mission_School_in_New_York" title="Russian Mission School in New York">Russian Mission School in New York</a> is located in Riverdale,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deutsch_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deutsch-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> on the grounds of the Russian Mission Residency.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Public_Library" title="New York Public Library">New York Public Library</a> (NYPL) operates three branches near Riverdale.
</p>
<ul><li>The Van Cortlandt branch is located at 3882 Cannon Place. The two-story, 5,800-square-foot (540&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) branch opened in 2019, replacing a smaller one-story branch a few blocks away, which opened in 1969 and consisted of a single room.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Riverdale branch is located at 5540 Mosholu Avenue. The branch opened in 1967, replacing a smaller library, and is located in a one-story L-shaped brick building surrounded by a garden.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Spuyten Duyvil branch is located at 650 West 235th Street. The one-story branch opened in 1971 and was designed by <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Cavaglieri" title="Giorgio Cavaglieri">Giorgio Cavaglieri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Riverdale_train_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Riverdale_train_station.jpg/250px-Riverdale_train_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Riverdale_train_station.jpg/375px-Riverdale_train_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Riverdale_train_station.jpg/500px-Riverdale_train_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="599" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Riverdale_train_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_(Metro-North_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Riverdale (Metro-North station)">Riverdale</a> <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North</a> station</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a>'s <a href="/wiki/IRT_Broadway%E2%80%93Seventh_Avenue_Line" title="IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line">IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line</a> (<span class="nowrap">1</span>&#32;train) stops at <a href="/wiki/Van_Cortlandt_Park%E2%80%93242nd_Street_(IRT_Broadway%E2%80%93Seventh_Avenue_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Cortlandt Park–242nd Street (IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line)">Van Cortlandt Park–242nd Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/238th_Street_(IRT_Broadway%E2%80%93Seventh_Avenue_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="238th Street (IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line)">238th Street</a>, and <a href="/wiki/231st_Street_(IRT_Broadway%E2%80%93Seventh_Avenue_Line)" class="mw-redirect" title="231st Street (IRT Broadway–Seventh Avenue Line)">231st Street</a> stations along Broadway.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North</a> <a href="/wiki/Commuter_railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Commuter railroad">commuter railroad</a> service is available at two stations, both on the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Line_(Metro-North)" title="Hudson Line (Metro-North)">Hudson Line</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil_(Metro-North_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spuyten Duyvil (Metro-North station)">Spuyten Duyvil</a> station, located underneath the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson_Parkway" title="Henry Hudson Parkway">Henry Hudson Parkway</a> and alongside the shore of the Harlem River at Edsall Avenue; and the <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_(Metro-North_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Riverdale (Metro-North station)">Riverdale</a> station, located between West 254th and West 255th Streets.
</p><p>By car, Riverdale is commonly reached by the Henry Hudson Parkway (<a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Route_9A" title="New York State Route 9A">NY 9A</a>) via the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson_Bridge" title="Henry Hudson Bridge">Henry Hudson Bridge</a>, and by <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Bronx)" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadway (Bronx)">Broadway</a> (<a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_9_in_New_York" title="U.S. Route 9 in New York">US 9</a>) via the <a href="/wiki/Broadway_Bridge_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway Bridge (Manhattan)">Broadway Bridge</a>.
</p><p>Bus service to Riverdale includes New York City's <a href="/wiki/MTA_Regional_Bus" class="mw-redirect" title="MTA Regional Bus">MTA Regional Bus</a> <a href="/wiki/Bx1_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bx1 (New York City bus)">Bx1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bx3_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bx3 (New York City bus)">Bx3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bx7_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bx7 (New York City bus)">Bx7</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bx9_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bx9 (New York City bus)">Bx9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bx10_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bx10 (New York City bus)">Bx10</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bx20_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bx20 (New York City bus)">Bx20</a>, <a href="/wiki/BxM1_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="BxM1 (New York City bus)">BxM1</a>, <a href="/wiki/BxM2_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="BxM2 (New York City bus)">BxM2</a>, <a href="/wiki/BxM3_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="BxM3 (New York City bus)">BxM3</a>, <a href="/wiki/BxM18_(New_York_City_bus)" class="mw-redirect" title="BxM18 (New York City bus)">BxM18</a> routes, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Bee-Line_Bus_System" title="Bee-Line Bus System">Bee-Line Bus System</a> routes <a href="/wiki/List_of_bus_routes_in_Westchester_County" title="List of bus routes in Westchester County">1, 2, 3, and 8</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Points_of_interest">Points of interest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Points of interest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">Parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wave_Hill" title="Wave Hill">Wave Hill</a>, a combination botanical garden and outdoor art gallery, is located in the so-called <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Hill,_Bronx" title="Hudson Hill, Bronx">Hudson Hill</a> overlooking the Hudson River.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Park" title="Gaelic Park">Gaelic Park</a>, has been owned by <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_College" title="Manhattan College">Manhattan College</a> since 1991, and is the home field of many of its sports teams, including lacrosse, soccer and softball, as well as the school's intramural sports.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Gaelic Park also is headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_GAA" title="New York GAA">New York GAA</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurling" title="Hurling">hurling</a> are played in the New York metropolitan area. Gaelic Park is the home field for <a href="/wiki/Rugby_United_New_York" title="Rugby United New York">Rugby United New York</a> in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Rugby" title="Major League Rugby">Major League Rugby</a>. Gaelic Park is located at West 240th Street.</li>
<li>Bell Tower Park next to the Henry Hudson Parkway has the <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Monument" title="Riverdale Monument">Riverdale Monument</a>, a  stone war memorial built in 1930.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Houses_of_worship">Houses of worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Houses of worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
 <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li>Chabad of Riverdale</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christ_Church_Riverdale" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ Church Riverdale">Christ Church Riverdale</a></li>
<li>Church of the Visitation</li>
<li>Congregation Tehillah<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Conservative_Synagogue_Adath_Israel_of_Riverdale" title="Conservative Synagogue Adath Israel of Riverdale">Conservative Synagogue Adath Israel of Riverdale</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edgehill_Church_at_Spuyten_Duyvil" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgehill Church at Spuyten Duyvil">Edgehill Church at Spuyten Duyvil</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Institute_of_Riverdale" title="Hebrew Institute of Riverdale">Hebrew Institute of Riverdale</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Jewish_Center" title="Riverdale Jewish Center">Riverdale Jewish Center</a></li>
<li>Riverdale Presbyterian Church<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Temple" title="Riverdale Temple">Riverdale Temple</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._Gabriel%27s_Roman_Catholic_Church,_Bronx,_N.Y." class="mw-redirect" title="St. Gabriel&#39;s Roman Catholic Church, Bronx, N.Y.">St. Gabriel's Roman Catholic Church</a></li>
<li>Saint Margaret of Cortona Church</li>
<li>St Peter's Greek Orthodox Church</li>
<li>Young Israel of Riverdale</li>
<li>Young Israel Ohab Tzedek</li></ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_organizations">Community organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Community organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bronx_Community_Board_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronx Community Board 8">Bronx Community Board 8</a> is a group of community members working under the mandate of the City Charter to monitor the delivery of city services, establish budget priorities, and influence land-use decisions.</li>
<li>Riverdale <a href="/wiki/Hatzalah" title="Hatzalah">Hatzalah</a> Volunteer Ambulance Corp.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> is supported by community donations, and offers fast, reliable medical treatment and transport free of charge.</li>
<li>Riverdale YM-YWHA is a community center for youth, adult and senior activities.</li>
<li>Riverdale Children's Theater is a local theatre company that has performed many pilot productions of musicals.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Derfner_Judaica_Museum" title="Derfner Judaica Museum">Derfner Judaica Museum</a> maintains a collection of approximately 1,400 objects used in traditional Jewish ceremonies and rituals, as well as Jewish art.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wave_Hill" title="Wave Hill">Wave Hill</a>, the former residence of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">Mark Twain</a> among others, is a botanical garden featuring two preserved historic mansions. It has exhibit spaces with a rotating series of art exhibitions, and performance spaces with a noted series of concerts.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverdale,_Bronx&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sean_Altman" title="Sean Altman">Sean Altman</a> (born 1961), musician, songwriter and founder of <a href="/wiki/Rockapella" title="Rockapella">Rockapella</a><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Baron_Ambrosia" title="Baron Ambrosia">Baron Ambrosia</a>, real name Justin Fornal, film director<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Appleton" title="William Henry Appleton">William Henry Appleton</a> (1814–1899), publisher, lived at <a href="/wiki/Wave_Hill_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wave Hill (New York)">Wave Hill</a><sup id="cite_ref-WaveHill_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaveHill-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Bart%C3%B3k" title="Béla Bartók">Béla Bartók</a> (1881–1945), composer<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ron_Blomberg" title="Ron Blomberg">Ron Blomberg</a> (born 1948), first <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a> in baseball history<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ted_Brown_(radio)" title="Ted Brown (radio)">Ted Brown</a> (1924–2005), radio personality<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Calder" title="Alexander Calder">Alexander Calder</a> (1898–1976), sculptor, lived in <a href="/wiki/Spuyten_Duyvil,_Bronx" title="Spuyten Duyvil, Bronx">Spuyten Duyvil</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Stirling_Calder" title="Alexander Stirling Calder">Alexander Stirling Calder</a> (1870–1945), sculptor, father of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Calder" title="Alexander Calder">Alexander Calder</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chris_Chambliss" title="Chris Chambliss">Chris Chambliss</a> (born 1948), former first baseman and hitting coach<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Seth_Farber" title="Seth Farber">Seth Farber</a>, rabbi and historian<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ella_Fitzgerald" title="Ella Fitzgerald">Ella Fitzgerald</a> (1917–1996), jazz singer<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Sidney Frey (1920–1968), <a href="/wiki/Audio_Fidelity_Records" title="Audio Fidelity Records">Audio Fidelity Records</a>, producer of the first stereo record<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fred_W._Friendly" title="Fred W. Friendly">Fred W. Friendly</a> (1915–1998), former president of <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a> (1903–1941), <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> baseball player<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jordan_Gelber" title="Jordan Gelber">Jordan Gelber</a> (born 1975), actor<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Goodman" title="Mark Goodman">Mark Goodman</a> (born 1952), one of the five original <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> VJs<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blu_Greenberg" title="Blu Greenberg">Blu Greenberg</a> (born 1936), writer specializing in <a href="/wiki/Modern_Orthodox_Judaism" title="Modern Orthodox Judaism">Modern Orthodox Judaism</a> and women's issues<sup id="cite_ref-Greenberg_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenberg-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Irving_Greenberg" title="Irving Greenberg">Irving Greenberg</a> (born 1933), <a href="/wiki/Modern_Orthodox_Judaism" title="Modern Orthodox Judaism">Modern Orthodox</a> rabbi, Jewish-American scholar and author<sup id="cite_ref-Greenberg_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greenberg-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nat_Holman" title="Nat Holman">Nat Holman</a> (1896–1995), Hall of Fame basketball player and <a href="/wiki/CCNY" class="mw-redirect" title="CCNY">CCNY</a> coach</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Evans_Hughes" title="Charles Evans Hughes">Charles Evans Hughes</a>, III (1915–1985), architect<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/H._Stuart_Hughes" title="H. Stuart Hughes">H. Stuart Hughes</a> (1916–1999), professor and activist<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Joel" title="Richard Joel">Richard Joel</a> (born 1950), President of <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva_University" title="Yeshiva University">Yeshiva University</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eric_Kandel" title="Eric Kandel">Eric Kandel</a> (born 1929), Columbia University neuroscientist, Nobel laureate<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eunice_Kennedy_Shriver" title="Eunice Kennedy Shriver">Eunice Kennedy</a> (1921–2009), founder of the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joan_Bennett_Kennedy" title="Joan Bennett Kennedy">Joan Bennett Kennedy</a> (born 1936), spouse of Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted Kennedy</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> (1917–1963), U.S. President, lived at 5040 Independence Avenue as a child<sup id="cite_ref-JFK_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFK-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kennedy,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.">Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.</a> (1888–1969), patriarch of the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennedy Family">Kennedy Family</a>, US Ambassador to the UK, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">SEC</a> Chairman</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Bernard_Kerik" title="Bernard Kerik">Bernard Kerik</a> (born 1955), former <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Commissioner" title="New York City Police Commissioner">New York City Police Commissioner</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>

Oliver Koppell</a> (born 1940), former New York State Attorney General, former member of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Council" title="New York City Council">New York City Council</a><sup id="cite_ref-Fieldston_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldston-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fiorello_H._La_Guardia" title="Fiorello H. La Guardia">Fiorello H. La Guardia</a> (1882–1947), <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_New_York_City" title="Mayor of New York City">Mayor of New York City</a> during the 1930s and 1940s<sup id="cite_ref-Fieldston_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldston-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_L._Lahey" title="John L. Lahey">John L. Lahey</a> (born 1946), president of <a href="/wiki/Quinnipiac_University" title="Quinnipiac University">Quinnipiac University</a><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lehmann-Haupt" title="Christopher Lehmann-Haupt">Christopher Lehmann-Haupt</a> (born 1934), journalist, critic and novelist<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Timothy_%22Speed%22_Levitch" class="mw-redirect" title="Timothy &quot;Speed&quot; Levitch">Timothy "Speed" Levitch</a> (born 1970), tour guide and voice actor<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jack_Lew" title="Jack Lew">Jack Lew</a> (born 1955), <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">United States Secretary of the Treasury</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sal_Maglie" title="Sal Maglie">Sal Maglie</a> (1917–1992), pitcher, played for the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a> (born 1931), baseball star<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Sister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_McEntee" title="Margaret McEntee">Margaret McEntee</a> (born 1935), Catholic nun and inspiration for <i><a href="/wiki/Doubt:_A_Parable" title="Doubt: A Parable">Doubt: A Parable</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tim_Morehouse" title="Tim Morehouse">Tim Morehouse</a> (born 1978), Olympic fencer<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tracy_Morgan" title="Tracy Morgan">Tracy Morgan</a> (born 1968), comedian and actor<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elie_Nadelman" title="Elie Nadelman">Elie Nadelman</a> (1882–1946), Polish/American sculptor<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Walbridge_Perkins" title="George Walbridge Perkins">George Walbridge Perkins</a> (1862–1920), first president of the <a href="/wiki/Palisades_Interstate_Park_Commission" title="Palisades Interstate Park Commission">Palisades Interstate Park Commission</a><sup id="cite_ref-WaveHill_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaveHill-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Raab" title="Jennifer Raab">Jennifer Raab</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Hunter_College" title="Hunter College">Hunter College</a><sup id="cite_ref-Fieldston_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldston-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ed_Rendell" title="Ed Rendell">Ed Rendell</a> (born 1944), <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor of Pennsylvania">Governor of Pennsylvania</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. <li><a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Theodore Roosevelt, Sr.">Theodore Roosevelt, Sr.</a> (1831–1878), banker and father of the U.S. President<sup id="cite_ref-WaveHill_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaveHill-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Rosenblatt" title="Jonathan Rosenblatt">Jonathan Rosenblatt</a>, former rabbi of the <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_Jewish_Center" title="Riverdale Jewish Center">Riverdale Jewish Center</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Herschel_Schacter" title="Herschel Schacter">Herschel Schacter</a>, rabbi</li>

Scheuer</a> (1920–2005), member of the House of Representatives<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. <li><a href="/wiki/David_Shapiro_(poet)" title="David Shapiro (poet)">David Shapiro</a> (born 1947), poet and literary critic<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carly_Simon" title="Carly Simon">Carly Simon</a> (born 1945), singer/songwriter<sup id="cite_ref-Fieldston_98-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldston-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joanna_Simon_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Joanna Simon (singer)">Joanna Simon</a> (born 1940), mezzo-soprano<sup id="cite_ref-Fieldston_98-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldston-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_L._Simon" title="Richard L. Simon">Richard L. Simon</a> (1899–1960), co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Simon_%26_Schuster" title="Simon &amp; Schuster">Simon &amp; Schuster</a><sup id="cite_ref-Fieldston_98-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fieldston-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/U_Thant" title="U Thant">U Thant</a> (1909–1974), former <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary-General">United Nations Secretary-General</a><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>
